Argument from the Sphere
Argument from sphere-plane tangency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the contact between a sphere and a plane demonstrates that surfaces are composed of indivisible atoms.

Core Idea
A sphere contacts a plane at a single indivisible point, showing matter is atomic.

The second argument uses a thought experiment with a perfect sphere on a flat plane. The initial contact is at a point, and as the sphere rotates, the line of contact sweeps across the plane, revealing that the entire surface is made of indivisible points. This supports the idea that matter is composed of atoms.

Guided Path
1
Visualize the scenario
Imagine a perfect sphere placed on a flat surface. The point of contact is where the sphere touches the plane.
2
Understand the rotation
When the sphere rotates, the contact point moves along a line. This line must be composed of the indivisible contact points.
3
Draw the conclusion
Since the contact point is indivisible, the line and the entire surface must be made of such indivisible units.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها ما يبتنى على أن محل النقطة جوهر لا يقبل الانقسام لقولهم النقطة موجودة، لأنها طرف الخط الموجود، وبها تماس الخطوط. فإن كان جوهراً فذاك، وإن كان عرضاً كان بالذات، أو بالواسطة حالاً في جوهر لا ينقسم، لئلا يلزم انقسام النقطة. وكقولهم : إذا وضعنا كرة حقيقية على سطح مستو إن قام خط على خط كانت المماسة بما لا ينقسم ثم إذا أديرت الكرة بتمامها على السطح، ومر الخط إلى آخر الخط ظهر عدم انقسام الأجزاء بأسرها، وثبت المطلوب، وكقولهم : قد ثبت أن الزاوية الحاصلة من مماسة الخط المستقيم لمحيط الدائرة أصغر الزوايا، فلا يقبل الانقسام فثبت الجزء.
And from them is what is based on the fact that the locus of a point is an indivisible substance, because they say: The point exists, for it is the extremity of the existing line, and by it lines touch. If it is a substance, then that is it; but if it is an accident, it would be either directly or mediately inherent in an indivisible substance, to avoid the necessity of the division of the point. And their statement: If we place a real sphere on a flat surface, when a line stands upon a line, the tangency is by what is indivisible; then if the sphere is rotated completely on the surface, and the line passes to the end of the line, the indivisibility of all the parts becomes apparent, and the desired is established. And their statement: It has been established that the angle formed by the tangency of a straight line to the circumference of a circle is the smallest of angles, so it does not accept division, thus the atom is established.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage presents three geometric arguments for the indivisible atom, all based on the nature of the point. First, the point exists as the extremity of a line and the means of tangency of lines; if it were an accident, it must inhere in an indivisible substance to avoid its own division. Second, when a true sphere contacts a plane surface, the contact is at a single indivisible point; rotating the sphere shows that the entire surface is composed of such indivisible points. Third, the angle formed by the tangent line and the circumference of a circle is the smallest possible angle and is indivisible, proving that its vertex is an indivisible atom. These arguments use geometry to support atomism.

Key Terms
كرة
سطح مستو
مماسة
خط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the rotation of the sphere demonstrate?
A) The sphere is smooth
B) The surface is composed of indivisible points
C) The sphere is divisible
D) The line is continuous

Key Takeaway
The sphere argument shows that tangential contact between a sphere and plane can only occur at an indivisible point, proving atoms.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every physical object you see, including your own body, is made of atom-like particles that only exist because Allah creates and sustains them at each instant, does your attachment to material things reflect that reality? How would your daily choices change if you truly lived with this awareness?
?
The mutakallimun used precise geometric arguments to prove that matter has a limit (indivisible parts). Where in your life have you acted as if things (your health, your wealth, your relationships) are endlessly divisible or unfailing? What would it look like to treat each moment and blessing as a finite, precious atom that could vanish in an instant?
?
This argument teaches that even a simple contact between sphere and plane reveals profound truths about creation. When you look at the world around you—a leaf, a drop of water—do you pause to see the signs of Allah's meticulous design, or do you pass by with indifference? Commit to one specific object or scene you will observe today with the eyes of a mutakallim, seeking to see the hand of the Creator in its smallest details.

Argument from the Minimal Angle
Argument from the minimal angle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the smallest possible angle in geometry proves the existence of indivisible atoms.

Core Idea
The smallest angle cannot be divided, so its vertex is an atom.

The third argument considers the angle formed when a straight line is tangent to a circle. This angle is claimed to be the smallest possible angle. Because it cannot be divided into smaller angles, its vertex must be an indivisible atom. This is a logical proof that space is discrete.

Guided Path
1
Understand the angle
The angle formed by the tangent line and the circle's circumference is extremely small, and it is said to be the smallest possible.
2
Consider divisibility
If this angle could be divided, there would be a smaller angle, contradicting its status as smallest.
3
Draw the conclusion
Therefore, the angle is indivisible, and its vertex is an atom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها ما يبتنى على أن محل النقطة جوهر لا يقبل الانقسام لقولهم النقطة موجودة، لأنها طرف الخط الموجود، وبها تماس الخطوط. فإن كان جوهراً فذاك، وإن كان عرضاً كان بالذات، أو بالواسطة حالاً في جوهر لا ينقسم، لئلا يلزم انقسام النقطة. وكقولهم : إذا وضعنا كرة حقيقية على سطح مستو إن قام خط على خط كانت المماسة بما لا ينقسم ثم إذا أديرت الكرة بتمامها على السطح، ومر الخط إلى آخر الخط ظهر عدم انقسام الأجزاء بأسرها، وثبت المطلوب، وكقولهم : قد ثبت أن الزاوية الحاصلة من مماسة الخط المستقيم لمحيط الدائرة أصغر الزوايا، فلا يقبل الانقسام فثبت الجزء.
And from them is what is based on the fact that the locus of a point is an indivisible substance, because they say: The point exists, for it is the extremity of the existing line, and by it lines touch. If it is a substance, then that is it; but if it is an accident, it would be either directly or mediately inherent in an indivisible substance, to avoid the necessity of the division of the point. And their statement: If we place a real sphere on a flat surface, when a line stands upon a line, the tangency is by what is indivisible; then if the sphere is rotated completely on the surface, and the line passes to the end of the line, the indivisibility of all the parts becomes apparent, and the desired is established. And their statement: It has been established that the angle formed by the tangency of a straight line to the circumference of a circle is the smallest of angles, so it does not accept division, thus the atom is established.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage presents three geometric arguments for the indivisible atom, all based on the nature of the point. First, the point exists as the extremity of a line and the means of tangency of lines; if it were an accident, it must inhere in an indivisible substance to avoid its own division. Second, when a true sphere contacts a plane surface, the contact is at a single indivisible point; rotating the sphere shows that the entire surface is composed of such indivisible points. Third, the angle formed by the tangent line and the circumference of a circle is the smallest possible angle and is indivisible, proving that its vertex is an indivisible atom. These arguments use geometry to support atomism.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The angle is actually divisible in higher mathematics.
Correction: In classical geometry, this angle was considered minimal; the argument is logical within that framework.

Key Takeaway
The minimal angle argument shows that the smallest geometric angle is indivisible, proving the existence of atoms.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This argument uses observation of geometry to affirm a deeper reality (atoms). Do you often examine the world around you for signs that lead to certainty about the unseen? Or do you go through life taking creation for granted, never pausing to see the Hand that set every limit?

The Four Types of Division in Kalam Atomism
Al-Maqasid explains the meaning of 'absolutely indivisible' and distinguishes types of division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what the mutakallimun mean by 'absolutely indivisible' and how they distinguish four types of division: cutting, breaking, imagination, and supposition.

Core Idea
The atom is indivisible in four distinct senses, but the intellect can still conceive of it.

The mutakallimun argued that bodies are composed of indivisible atoms. To clarify what 'indivisible' means, they specify four types of division: physical and mental. This passage distinguishes them and explains the limitations of the estimative faculty compared to the intellect.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the four terms: قطعاً, كسراً, وهماً, فرضاً.
The passage uses concise kalam style.
2
Identify the four types of division
Find each type and note how the author defines it: cutting (cut) requires a tool, breaking (break) does not, both lead to actual separation.
3
Distinguish physical from mental division
Understand that cutting and breaking are physical; imagination and supposition are mental. The estimative faculty (وهم) is limited, but the intellect (عقل) can conceive infinite divisions.
The intellect's divisions are universal, not actual.
4
Reflect on the meaning of 'absolutely indivisible'
Consider why the atom is said to be indivisible in all four senses. The point is that no actual or mental division can break the atom, though the intellect can still conceive of it as a whole.
This prevents misunderstanding that the atom is divisible by thought.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أي الطريق الثاني للمتكلمين إثبات جوهر في الجسم لا يقبل الانقسام أصلاً، أى لا قطعاً، ولا كسراً، ولا وهماً، ولا فرضاً. والفرق بينهما أن القطع يفتقر إلى آلة نفاذة، بخلاف الكسر، ثم إنهما يؤديان إلى الافتراق بخلاف الوهمي والفرضي. والوهمي إذا أريد به ما يكون بمعونة القوة الوهمية، التي هي سلطان القوى الحسية، قد يقف أي لا يقدر على تقسيمات غير متناهية لما تقرر عندهم من تناهي أفعال القوى الجسمانية بخلاف فرض العقل فإن العقل يتعلق بالكليات المشتملة على الصغيرة والكبيرة والمتناهية وغير المتناهية.
That is, the second way for the mutakallimun is establishing an atom in the body that does not accept division at all, i.e., not by cutting, not by breaking, not by imagination, and not by supposition. The difference between them is that cutting requires a penetrating instrument, unlike breaking; then both lead to separation, unlike the imaginary and suppositional. And the imaginary, if intended as what is by means of the estimative faculty, which is the sultan of the sensory powers, may stop, i.e., it is not capable of infinite divisions, due to what has been established with them about the finitude of the actions of bodily powers, unlike the supposition of the intellect, for the intellect pertains to universals that include the small and the large, the finite and the infinite.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage clarifies what the mutakallimun mean by 'an atom that does not accept division at all' (لا يقبل الانقسام أصلاً). They specify four types of division: (1) by cutting (قطعاً) with a tool, (2) by breaking (كسراً) without a tool, (3) by imagination (وهماً) via the estimative faculty, and (4) by supposition (فرضاً) via the intellect. The first two result in actual separation, while the latter two are mental. The estimative faculty (القوة الوهمية) is limited and cannot divide infinitely, but the intellect can conceive of infinite division and includes all universals. Thus, the atom is indivisible in all four senses, but the intellect can still suppose it.

Key Terms
قطع
كسر
وهم
فرض
قوة وهمية
عقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The atom is not divisible even by intellect; i.e., the intellect cannot conceive of it as having parts.
Correction: The text says the atom is not divisible by supposition (فرضاً) in the sense of actual mental separation, but the intellect can still conceive of it in a universal sense, including the idea of infinite division.

Checkpoint
What does the estimative faculty (القوة الوهمية) lack that the intellect possesses?
A) Ability to divide physically
B) Ability to conceive of infinite divisions
C) Ability to separate
D) Ability to imagine

Key Takeaway
The atom is indivisible in all four senses—cutting, breaking, imagination, and supposition—but the intellect can still conceive of infinite divisions in a universal way.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You rely on your estimative faculty every day—your instincts, gut feelings, and sensory-based judgments. When have you confused your inability to imagine something with its impossibility? How can you train your intellect to overrule your imagination when revelation speaks of realities beyond your senses?
?
The intellect can conceive of infinite divisions of an atom even though the atom is indivisible. What does this tell you about the gap between your mental capacities and the actual nature of things? Are there beliefs about Allah that you have rejected because you cannot imagine them, even though your intellect should affirm them? What would it take for you to humble your imagination before your intellect and submit to the truth?
?
You are finite, yet your intellect can reach universal truths. How often do you settle for the limits of your senses rather than striving for intellectual certainty? This lesson forces you to choose: will you remain confined to what your senses can cut, break, or imagine, or will you rise to the supposition of the intellect that embraces the infinite? Commit to one concrete step today to discipline your thinking.

Objection: Proving the Atom Does Not Prove Composition, and Answer
Al-Maqasid responds to the objection that proving an indivisible atom does not prove that bodies are composed of atoms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author answers the objection that proving an indivisible atom does not automatically prove that bodies are composed of atoms.

Core Idea
Even if proving the atom doesn't directly prove composition, it refutes the philosophers' claim of impossibility.

In this passage, Sanusi addresses a subtle objection: even if we succeed in proving that indivisible atoms exist, does that necessarily prove that bodies are actually made up of them? The objector says no. Sanusi’s answer is honest and careful, showing that the kalam argument has sufficient force.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the Arabic passage once to understand the objection and answer. Notice the concise style.
The objection is in the form 'fain qīla...'
2
Identify the concession and answer
The author concedes the point ('naʿam') but then gives two reasons why proving the atom still matters. Identify both reasons.
The first reason is that it refutes the philosophers; the second is that some arguments do imply composition.
3
Reflect on the strategy
Consider why the author admits the objection has force, yet still defends the atom argument. What does this tell you about kalam methodology?
This shows that kalam scholars are careful not to overclaim their proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : إثبات الجوهر الفرد لا يفيد المطلوب. أعني تركب الجسم منها. قلنا : نعم إلا أنه يكفي لدفع ما يدعيه الفلاسفة من امتناعه، على أن بعض الوجوه المذكورة مما يفيد أصل المطلوب.
If it is said: Establishing the individual atom does not benefit the desired, namely the composition of the body from them. We say: Yes, but it suffices to repel what the philosophers claim of its impossibility, and some of the mentioned aspects do benefit the very desired.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection: even if we prove the existence of an indivisible atom, does that prove that bodies are actually composed of such atoms? The author concedes that it does not directly prove composition, but it is sufficient to refute the philosophers' claim that atoms are impossible. Moreover, some of the earlier arguments (such as those based on the equality of mountain and mustard seed) do directly imply that bodies are made of atoms. Thus, the project of proving the atom is not in vain.

Key Terms

مطلوب
تركب
فلاسفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) It suffices to refute the philosophers' denial
C) It is irrelevant
D) It disproves the atom

Key Takeaway
The kalam argument for the atom is not solely to prove composition but to refute the philosophers' denial of atoms, and some arguments do imply composition directly.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In this passage, the author concedes a partial objection but still finds value in his argument. When you encounter a critique of your beliefs, do you quickly abandon them or do you examine whether the critique is partial and whether your argument still holds value? Write down a specific time you faced such a situation.
?
The philosophers claimed impossibility without proof. Is there a belief you hold as impossible that you have never truly examined? What would it take to honestly reconsider it?
?
The author says 'it suffices to repel what the philosophers claim'. Are you content with merely refuting false claims, or do you also seek to establish positive truth? How can you move from defense to construction in your own faith?

The Second Way: Proving the Indivisible Atom
Details the second way to prove the indivisible atom and answers an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the mutakallimun's second way of proving the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard), including the types of division it resists and the response to the objection that such proof does not directly establish the composition of bodies.

Core Idea
The indivisible atom cannot be divided by any means—physical or mental—refuting the philosophers' denial.

The mutakallimun (Islamic theologians) developed multiple arguments to prove the existence of the indivisible atom (jawhar fard). This passage presents their second way, which focuses on the atom's absolute indivisibility. It clarifies the different senses of 'division'—cutting, breaking, imagining, and supposing—and then addresses a key objection: does proving the atom prove that bodies are composed of them? Let's explore the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal English translation to grasp the overall meaning.
Notice the Arabic terms for different types of division: قطع, كسر, وهم, فرض.
2
Identify the four types of division
The passage lists four ways something might be divided: by cutting (qaṭʿ), by breaking (kars), by imagination (wahm), and by supposition (fard). Understand the physical vs. mental distinction.
Cutting requires a tool; breaking doesn't. Both lead to separation, unlike imaginary and suppositional divisions.
3
Understand the limitation of the estimative faculty
The passage explains that the estimative faculty (al-wahm) cannot perform infinite divisions because it is a bodily power with finite capacity, unlike the intellect which can conceive of infinite divisions.
This distinction justifies why the atom is indivisible even in imagination.
4
Examine the objection and answer
An objector says proving the indivisible atom doesn't prove bodies are composed of such atoms. The author concedes but argues it suffices to refute the philosophers' claim of impossibility, and some aspects of the proof do establish composition.
This shows the strategic purpose of the argument within the broader kalam system.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider how this argument fits into the mutakallimun's overall atomic theory and their debate with philosophers.
The proof doesn't need to do everything—it serves to rebut a specific claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أي الطريق الثاني للمتكلمين إثبات جوهر في الجسم لا يقبل الانقسام أصلاً، أى لا قطعاً، ولا كسراً، ولا وهماً، ولا فرضاً والفرق بينهما أن القطع يفتقر إلى آلة نفاذة، بخلاف الكسر، ثم إنهما يؤديان إلى الافتراق بخلاف الوهمي، والفرضي، والوهمي إذا أريد به ما يكون بمعونة القوة الوهمية، التي هي سلطان القوى الحسية، قد يقف أي لا يقدر على تقسيمات غير متناهية لما تقرر عندهم من تناهي أفعال القوى الجسمانية بخلاف فرض العقل فإن العقل يتعلق بالكليات المشتملة على الصغيرة والكبيرة والمتناهية، وغير المتناهية. فإن قيل: إثبات الجوهر الفرد لا يفيد المطلوب أعني تركب الجسم منها. قلنا: نعم إلا أنه يكفي لدفع ما يدعيه الفلاسفة من امتناعه، على أن بعض الوجوه المذكورة مما يفيد أصل المطلوب.
That is, the second way for the mutakallimun is to prove an atom (jawhar) in the body that does not accept division at all, i.e., not by cutting, nor by breaking, nor by imagination (wahm), nor by supposition (fard). The difference between them is that cutting requires a penetrating instrument, unlike breaking; then both lead to separation, unlike the imaginary and the suppositional. The imaginary, if intended as that which occurs with the help of the estimative faculty (al-quwwa al-wahmiyya), which is the ruler of the sensory powers, may stop—i.e., it is not capable of infinite divisions, because it is established among them that the acts of bodily powers are finite, unlike the supposition of the intellect, for the intellect deals with universals that include the small and the large, the finite and the infinite. So if it is said: 'The proof of the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard) does not yield the desired conclusion, namely the composition of the body from it,' we say: 'Yes, but it suffices to refute what the philosophers claim of its impossibility, and indeed some of the aforementioned aspects yield the original desired conclusion.'
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage defines the second way (al-ṭarīq al-thānī) used by the mutakallimun to prove the existence of the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard). It begins by specifying that this atom does not accept division in any sense: not by cutting (qaṭʿan) which requires a tool, not by breaking (kasran), not by imagination (wahman) using the estimative faculty, and not by intellectual supposition (fardan). The author distinguishes these types of division: cutting and breaking are physical and lead to actual separation, whereas imaginary and suppositional divisions are mental. The estimative faculty (al-wahm) is limited and cannot perform infinite divisions because it is a bodily power, whereas the intellect (al-ʿaql) can conceive of infinite divisions in a universal sense. The passage then presents an objection: proving the indivisible atom does not directly prove that bodies are composed of such atoms (the desired conclusion). The author answers that even if it doesn't directly prove composition, it suffices to refute the philosophers' claim that such an atom is impossible. Moreover, some of the other arguments (mentioned later) do establish the composition directly.

Key Terms
جوهر فرد
انقسام
قطع
كسر
وهم
فرض
قوة وهمية
متكلمون
فلاسفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Proving the indivisible atom is useless because it doesn't directly prove that bodies are composed of such atoms.
Correction: The author agrees it doesn't directly prove composition, but it refutes the philosophers' claim of impossibility, and some aspects of the argument do establish composition.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a reason why the estimative faculty (al-wahm) cannot perform infinite divisions?
A) Because it is a bodily power with finite capacity
B) Because it is opposed to the intellect
C) Because it deals with universals
D) Because it requires an instrument

Key Takeaway
The indivisible atom is proven by its absolute resistance to division in all senses, and while this does not directly prove body composition, it suffices to refute the philosophical denial of its possibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The mutakallimun argued that even your imagination cannot divide the indivisible atom because your estimative faculty is finite. In what areas of your life have you assumed your mental powers are infinite, and how might that assumption be leading you to overlook limits that should humble you before your Creator?
?
The philosophers denied the atom because they thought it impossible. Are there truths about God or the unseen that you have dismissed simply because they do not fit within the categories your mind expects? What would it cost you to remain open to possibilities beyond your intellectual frameworks?
?
The atom resists division in every sense—physical and mental. Do you have any core beliefs that you treat as indivisible, too sacred to be questioned even in supposition? Is your reluctance to examine them rooted in faith or in fear? What might happen if you allowed them to be truly tested by the intellect?

Time, Perpetuity, and Eternity in Islamic Philosophy
Defines time, perpetuity, eternity and quotes Aristotle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophical distinctions between zaman (time), dahr (perpetuity), and sarmad (eternity), and Aristotle's definition of time as the measure of motion.

Core Idea
Time is not a god nor discrete moments; it is the continuous measure of motion.

Having discussed the indivisible part, the author now turns to clarifying the concept of time. He begins with common usages and then lays out precise philosophical distinctions between time, perpetuity, and eternity. The passage also presents Aristotle's influential definition, which the author critiques implicitly by rejecting discrete moments. This lesson will help you navigate these key terms and arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage first, then the translation. Notice how the author moves from lexical examples to philosophical distinctions.
Pay attention to the three terms: زمان, دهر, سرمد.
2
Understand the three relational definitions
The passage defines zaman, dahr, and sarmad based on whether the relation involves change or constancy. Identify each pair (changing/constant) and note the corresponding term.
Time (zaman) = changing to constant; dahr = constant to changing; sarmad = constant to constant.
3
Analyze Aristotle's definition
Aristotle argues that time is the measure of the motion of the outermost sphere. Follow the reasoning: time varies → it is a quantity → not discrete (no atoms) → continuous but non-stable → measure of a non-stable form (motion).
This definition contrasts with the atomistic view mentioned earlier.
4
Connect to the broader theological context
Consider how these definitions relate to debates about creation, eternity, and divine attributes. The author uses these distinctions to clarify theological positions.
The passage is part of a larger discussion on the indivisible part and motion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنه زمان الحصاد وزمان الشباب وزمان الجاهلية وجمع الزمان أزمنة، أي أقسام وفصول ونقول: الأزمنة القديمة والأزمنة الحديثة. والزمان في أساطير اليونانيين هو الاله الذي ينضج الأشياء ويوصلها الى نهايتها .. والفرق بين الزمان والدهر والسرمد: أن نسبة المتغير إلى الثابت هي الزمان ونسبة الثابت إلى المتغير هي الدهر، ونسبة الثابت إلى الثابت هي السرمد لقد زعم أرسطو أن الزمان مقدار حركة الفلك الأعظم وذلك لأن الزمان متفاوت زيادة ونقصاناً فهو إذن كم وليس كماً منفصلاً لامتناع الجوهر الفرد فلا يكون مركباً من آنات متتالية فهو إذن كم متصل، إلا أنه غير قار، فهو إذن مقدار لهيئة غير قارة وهي الحركة.
And from it [the word zaman] is [used in] 'time of harvest', 'time of youth', and 'time of ignorance'; the plural of zaman is azmina, meaning sections and seasons. We say: ancient times and modern times. And time in Greek mythology is the god that ripens things and brings them to their end.. And the difference between time (zaman), perpetuity (dahr), and eternity (sarmad) is that the relation of the changing to the constant is time, the relation of the constant to the changing is dahr, and the relation of the constant to the constant is sarmad. Aristotle claimed that time is the measure of the motion of the outermost sphere, because time varies in increase and decrease, so it is a quantity, not a discrete quantity because of the impossibility of the atom, so it is not composed of successive moments; it is thus a continuous quantity, except that it is non-stable, so it is a measure of a non-stable form, namely motion.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage provides lexical and philosophical definitions of time (zaman). It begins with examples of usage: 'time of harvest', 'time of youth', 'time of ignorance'. It notes that the plural is azmina, meaning sections/seasons. Then it mentions the Greek mythological view of time as a god. The key part is the distinction between three terms: zaman, dahr, and sarmad. Zaman (time) is the relation of the changing (mutaghayyir) to the constant (thabit). Dahr (perpetuity) is the relation of the constant to the changing. Sarmad (eternity) is the relation of the constant to the constant. This is a common philosophical distinction. Then the author reports Aristotle's definition: time is the measure (miqdar) of the motion of the outermost sphere (the celestial sphere). Aristotle argues that time varies in increase and decrease, so it is a quantity (kamm). But it is not a discrete quantity (kamm munsil) because there are no indivisible atoms (jawhar fard) according to Aristotle; hence it is not composed of successive moments (anatin mutataliya). Rather, it is a continuous quantity (kamm muttasil), but non-stable (ghayr qarr). Therefore, it is a measure of a non-stable form, namely motion. This passage serves to clarify the concept of time in relation to the earlier argument for the indivisible part, rejecting Aristotle's continuity view.

الدهر

أرسطو
الكم المتصل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Time (zaman), perpetuity (dahr), and eternity (sarmad) are interchangeable or refer to the same concept.
Correction: The passage clearly distinguishes them by the relation involved: zaman links the changing to the constant, dahr links the constant to the changing, and sarmad links the constant to the constant.

Checkpoint

A) Time is the relation of the constant to the changing.
B) Time is the relation of the changing to the constant.
C) Time is the relation of the constant to the constant.
D) Time is the measure of motion.

Key Takeaway
Time (zaman) is the relation of the changing to the constant, distinct from perpetuity and eternity, and Aristotle defines it as the continuous measure of motion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

When you consider that time is the measure of motion, and your own actions are motions, what does your use of time reveal about your priorities? Ask yourself: Am I investing my time in what perishes or in what remains with the Eternal?
?
The Greek myth portrayed time as a god that ripens things. How have you unconsciously treated time as a force independent of Allah? Repent of that mindset and commit to seeing time as a created measure of change, subject to Allah alone.

The Point Proves an Indivisible Substance
First proof: the point's existence entails an indivisible substance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the existence of a point entails an indivisible substance in classical kalam.

Core Idea
The point proves an indivisible substance exists.

This lesson presents the first proof for an indivisible substance (al-jawhar alladhi la yuqbal al-inqisam) in classical kalam. The argument starts from a simple observation about points and lines. By examining what a point is and how it relates to substances and accidents, the theologian builds a rigorous proof that there must be an indivisible foundation of matter.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing, then read the translation. Let the flow of the argument settle in your mind.
The argument is dense but proceeds step by step.
2
Identify the stages of the proof
Notice how the proof first establishes the existence of the point, then classifies it as substance or accident, and finally deduces that an indivisible substance must exist.
Each stage builds on the previous one.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider why this proof was important for kalam atomism. It shows that even common geometric concepts imply a substratum that cannot be divided.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأول: أن النقطة موجودة لأنها طرف الخط الموجود ، وطرف الموجود موجود بالضرورة ولأنه شيء به يتماس الخطوط، وتماسها بالعدم الصرف محال، ولأنها ذات وضع ، أي يشار إليها إشارة حسية بأنها هنالك ، وهذا في المعدوم محال، ثم إنها إما أن تكون جوهراً كما هو رأي المتكلمين، أو عرضاً، وحينئذ يفتقر إلى جوهر يحل فيه بالذات إن لم تجوز قيام العرض أو بالواسطة إن جوزاه، وذلك الجوهر يمتنع أن يكون منقسماً وإلا لزم انقسام النقطة، ضرورة انقسام الحال بانقسام المحل، هذا خلف . فأياً ما كان يثبت جوهر لا يقبل الانقسام، وهو المطلوب.
First: The point (النقطة) exists because it is the extremity of an existing line, and the extremity of an existing thing necessarily exists, and because it is a thing by which lines touch, and their touching by pure non-existence is impossible, and because it possesses position (وضع), meaning it can be pointed to by sensory indication as being there, and this is impossible for a non-existent. Then it is either a substance (جوهر) as is the view of the theologians (المتكلمين), or an accident (عرض). In that case it requires a substance in which it inheres directly if one does not permit the subsistence of an accident independently, or indirectly if one permits it. That substance cannot be divisible, otherwise the division of the point would follow necessarily due to the division of the accident with the division of the subject. This is a contradiction. So in any case, an indivisible substance is established, which is what was sought.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage presents the first proof for the existence of an indivisible substance (جوهر لا يقبل الانقسام). The argument proceeds from the reality of the point (النقطة). It states that the point exists because it is the extremity of an existing line, and the extremity of something existing must itself exist. Moreover, the point is that by which lines touch, and touching between existents cannot occur through pure non-existence. The point also has position, meaning it can be sensibly indicated as being there, which is impossible for something non-existent. These considerations show the point is real. Then the argument examines the nature of the point: it must be either a substance (جوهر) — as the theologians hold — or an accident (عرض). If it is an accident, it requires a substance in which to inhere, either directly (if accidents cannot subsist independently) or indirectly (if they can). In either case, that substance must be indivisible, because if it were divisible, the point would also be divisible (since the accident divides with the division of its subject). But a divisible point leads to an infinite regress or contradiction. Therefore, an indivisible substance is established, which is the desired conclusion.

Key Terms
النقطة
جوهر
عرض
لا يقبل الانقسام
طرف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Points are merely conceptual and do not have real existence.
Correction: The proof argues points are real because they are extremities of existing lines and have position, which cannot be said of non-existents.

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, what follows if the point were an accident inhering in a divisible substance?
A) The point would be indivisible.
B) The point would also be divisible.
C) The point would be a substance.
D) The point would not exist.

Key Takeaway
The existence of a point, as the extremity of a line, logically necessitates an indivisible substance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This proof begins with something as simple as a point and concludes with a profound reality: an indivisible substance. Do you treat the small signs in your life—the things you take for granted—as starting points for awe and contemplation, or do you pass them by without thought? What one small sign will you commit to reflecting on today?
?
The argument forces you to accept that even a point cannot be imaginary. When you recite 'Allahu Akbar' (God is Greater), do you truly believe that every single thing in existence testifies to His greatness, or do you let the words become hollow? What would change in your prayer if you genuinely saw each moment as a proof of divine reality?
?
The proof uses logic and reason to establish a foundational truth. Have you ever felt the weight of rational certainty in your faith, or have you relied only on emotion and tradition? Will you now make a deliberate effort to study the intellectual proofs of your belief, not as an academic exercise but as a means to deepen your conviction and action?

Proof: Sphere on a Plane Forces Indivisible Parts
Second proof for indivisible part via sphere-plane tangency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical argument that the genuine tangency of a sphere and a plane requires an indivisible contact part, establishing the existence of indivisible substances.

Core Idea
Genuine sphere-plane contact demands an indivisible part.

This lesson presents a second proof from kalam that an indivisible part must exist. The argument uses geometry: if a sphere touches a plane, the contact area cannot be divisible, otherwise the sphere would have a flat surface. This forces the existence of an indivisible part, which is either a substance or an accident. The proof relies on logical deduction from the nature of perfect geometrical shapes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the logical structure: assumption, conditional, contradiction, conclusion.
The text is concise; each phrase carries weight.
2
Identify the key assumption
The proof assumes a real sphere (كرة حقيقية) and a real surface (سطح حقيقي). This is crucial for the argument to work.
These are ideal geometric entities, not physical approximations.
3
Understand the conditional reasoning
If the contact part were divisible, then the sphere's surface would contain a straight line or a plane, contradicting its being a real sphere. Therefore, the contact part must be indivisible.
This is a proof by contradiction (reductio ad absurdum).
4
Consider the conclusion and its implications
The indivisible part is either a substance (جوهر) — the desired conclusion — or an accident (عرض). Even if it is an accident, it still requires an indivisible substance to inhere in.
The argument does not stop at the contact part; it links to the broader atomism doctrine.
5
Reflect on the rotation argument
Rotating the sphere on the surface shows that the entire surface is composed of indivisible parts, reinforcing the conclusion.
This extends the proof from a single point to the whole surface.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني: أنا إذا وضعنا كرة حقيقية على سطح حقيقي مماسة بجزء لا يقبل الانقسام وإلا لكان في سطح الكرة خط مستقيم أو سطح مستو فلا تكون الكرة كرة حقيقية. هذا خلف فذلك الجزء إما جوهر وهو المطلوب، أو عرض وفيه المطلوب ، ثم إذا أدرنا تلك الكرة على ذلك السطح ظهر كون سطحها من أجزاء لا تتجزأ، وبه يتم المقصود، والقول بامتناع الكرة أو السطح أو تماسها مكابرة ومخالفة لقواعدهم .
Second: If we place a real sphere (كرة حقيقية) on a real surface (سطح حقيقي) touching it by a part that does not accept division, otherwise there would be in the surface of the sphere a straight line or a plane, and then the sphere would not be a real sphere. This is a contradiction. So that part is either a substance, which is what is sought, or an accident, and the sought is also in it. Then if we rotate that sphere on that surface, it becomes apparent that its surface is composed of indivisible parts, and by this the purpose is accomplished. The claim that the sphere, the surface, or their touching is impossible is obstinacy and contradicts their principles.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof for an indivisible substance, based on the contact between a sphere and a plane. The argument assumes a real sphere (كرة حقيقية) and a real surface (سطح حقيقي). For the sphere to genuinely touch the surface, the contact must occur at a part that does not accept division. If the contact area were divisible, then the contact would involve a line or a plane on the sphere's surface, meaning the sphere would have a flat part, contradicting its perfectly spherical nature. Therefore, the part of contact must be indivisible. This indivisible part is either a substance (جوهر) — the desired conclusion — or an accident (عرض), which would still require an indivisible substance to inhere in. Additionally, rotating the sphere on the surface reveals that the sphere's surface itself must be composed of indivisible parts to maintain continuous smooth contact. The argument dismisses any denial of the possibility of a genuine sphere or surface as obstinacy contradicting the philosophers' own geometrical principles.

Key Terms
كرة
سطح
مماسة
جزء لا يتجزأ
جوهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This proof is about empirical observations of physical spheres and surfaces.
Correction: The proof is logical and deals with ideal geometric entities; it does not depend on empirical measurement.

Checkpoint
What would happen if the sphere touched the surface over a divisible area according to the second proof?
A) The sphere would be a perfect sphere.
B) The sphere would have a line or a plane on its surface.
C) The sphere would be indivisible.
D) The sphere would disappear.

Key Takeaway
The tangency of a sphere and a plane logically necessitates an indivisible contact part, which supports the existence of indivisible substances.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This proof shows that our common-sense assumption of infinite divisibility may be logically impossible. Is there an area of your life where you have assumed something to be true simply because it felt right, without checking the logical foundations? What would it cost you to question that assumption today?
?
The argument forces you to accept an indivisible contact point even if you cannot see it. Are you willing to accept truths that your senses cannot confirm but reason demands? What do you typically trust more: your intuition or logical necessity?
?
The proof uses a purely hypothetical scenario — a perfect sphere and plane — to reach a conclusion about reality. Do you dismiss hypothetical arguments in your own reasoning? When have you rejected a difficult truth because you thought it was 'just theoretical'? How can you change that habit starting today?

Third Proof: Line on a Line
Third proof: a line crossing another line reveals indivisible parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the geometric proof that lines are composed of indivisible parts, based on a line crossing another line.

Core Idea
A line's pivot reveals its atomic composition.

In this lesson, we examine the third proof from the kalam tradition for the existence of indivisible parts. Using a simple geometric scenario of one line standing on another, the proof shows that the point of contact must be indivisible, and thus the lines themselves are composed of such parts. This argument reinforces the atomist doctrine against continuous theories.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
2
Visualize the geometry
Imagine a line standing on another and pivoting from one side to the other. Notice how the contact point must be indivisible.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Why does the pivot demonstrate composition from indivisible parts? Consider the logic: what falls on the indivisible is itself indivisible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث: أنه إذا قام خط على خط في أحد جانبيه لقبه بجزء لا ينقسم، ثم إذا مر عليه إلى الجانب الآخر ظهر تألفه من أجزاء لا تتجزأ، ضرورة أن ما يقع عليه غير المنقسم غير منقسم.
Third: If a line stands on another line on one of its sides, it touches it by a part that does not divide; then when it passes over it to the other side, it becomes apparent that it is composed of indivisible parts, necessarily because what falls on the indivisible is indivisible.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof for the existence of indivisible parts, based on the behavior of intersecting lines. The scenario: one line (خط) stands on another line, making contact at a point. When the first line pivots from one side to the other, the contact point must be an indivisible part. If the point were divisible, the line would have to pass through intermediate divisible parts, but the argument asserts that what falls upon the indivisible (i.e., the point of contact) is itself indivisible. Consequently, both lines must be composed of indivisible parts (أجزاء لا تتجزأ). This is a geometrical argument that lines, and by extension bodies, are made up of discrete, indivisible units.

Key Terms
خط
جزء لا ينقسم
أجزاء لا تتجزأ
غير منقسم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Lines are infinitely divisible and have no indivisible parts.
Correction: This proof shows that lines must be composed of indivisible parts because contact between lines occurs at an indivisible point.

Checkpoint
In the third proof, what does the pivot of a line on another line demonstrate?
A) That lines are continuous.
B) That lines are composed of indivisible parts.
C) That points are accidents.
D) That motion is impossible.

Key Takeaway
A line's pivot on another line reveals that lines are composed of indivisible parts (أجزاء لا تتجزأ).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This proof shows that everything is composed of indivisible parts, and that what falls on the indivisible must itself be indivisible. In your spiritual life, what indivisible core belief have you built your faith upon? Consider: if that belief were proven false by its contact with a deeper truth, would your entire faith shatter? Have you guarded it with rigorous understanding or just accepted it blindly?
?
The proof uses a simple physical pivot to reveal a hidden reality. Where in your daily life is there a 'pivot'—a moment of decision or reaction—that reveals the true composition of your character? Are you composed of virtues like patience and honesty in small, indivisible acts? What does your smallest reaction to inconvenience reveal about the atoms of your soul?
?
The argument concludes necessarily that what falls on the indivisible is indivisible. Euclid's Angle: Proof of the Indivisible
Fourth proof: Euclid's minimal angle shows an indivisible part.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Euclid's theorem about the smallest possible angle is used to prove the existence of an indivisible substance (atom).

Core Idea
Euclid's minimal angle cannot be halved, implying an indivisible part.

This proof brings geometry into theology: the smallest angle possible, formed by a tangent line touching a circle, must be indivisible. From that indivisible entity, the existence of an indivisible substance (jawhar) is deduced, supporting the atomic theory of kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof passage
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Note how the argument unfolds: a geometric fact is stated, then its theological implication is drawn.
The proof relies on Euclid's accepted theorem.
2
Understand the geometric premise
Euclid proved that the angle between a tangent line and a circle's circumference is the smallest possible angle. Why can't there be a smaller angle? The key is that any smaller angle would require the line to cut the circle, which it does not.
Visualize: a tangent just touches the circle at one point.
3
Follow the logical deduction
If that angle were divisible, its half would be even smaller, contradicting its definition. Hence it is indivisible. This indivisible entity must be either a substance or an accident. Either way, an indivisible substance exists.
The argument moves from geometry to ontology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع: أنه برهن أقليدس على أن الزاوية الحاصلة مماسة الخط المستقيم لمحيط الدائرة أصغر ما يمكن من الزوايا، فبالضرورة لا يقبل الانقسام، وإلا لكان نصفها أصغر منه ، فذلك الأمر الغير المنقسم، إما جوهر أو حال فيه ، وفيه المطلوب.
Fourth: Euclid proved that the angle resulting from a straight line tangent to the circumference of a circle is the smallest possible of angles, so necessarily it does not accept division; otherwise, half of it would be smaller than it. So that indivisible thing is either a substance or something in which it inheres, and the sought is in it.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof for the existence of an indivisible substance, drawing from Euclid's geometry. Euclid demonstrated that the angle formed by a straight line tangent to a circle's circumference is the smallest possible angle. This angle must be indivisible, because if it were divisible, half of it would be an even smaller angle, contradicting its definition as the smallest. Therefore, that indivisible entity is either a substance (جوهر) or an accident (عرض) inhering in a substance. In either case, an indivisible substance is established. This proof uses a mathematical theorem to argue for atomism.

Key Terms
أقليدس
زاوية
مماسة
غير منقسم
جوهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof is an empirical measurement of a real angle.
Correction: The proof is a logical and mathematical argument, not an empirical one. It assumes Euclid's theorem is true and deduces metaphysical consequences.

Checkpoint
According to the fourth proof, why must the smallest angle be indivisible?
A) Because it is a point.
B) Because halving it would yield a smaller angle.
C) Because it is a line.
D) Because it is a substance.

Key Takeaway
Euclid's geometric demonstration of a minimal angle provides a rational proof for the existence of an indivisible substance, a cornerstone of kalam atomism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Euclid's proof shows that even the smallest angle is indivisible. Reflect: in your daily life, what 'small' sins do you consider divisible — that you can cut in half and still be okay? How does this proof challenge that assumption?
?
The proof concludes that the indivisible thing is either a substance or an accident. In your spiritual life, what accidents (non-essential traits) do you cling to as if they were substances? Are you treating worldly things as permanent when they are only temporary?
?
The smallest possible angle points to an indivisible reality behind perception. Have you ever paused to recognize that your own perceptions of 'small' things are limited? How can this realization increase your awareness of Allah's infinite knowledge — that He sees every indivisible moment of your life?

Philosophers' Objection and Author's Response on Tangency
Refutation of philosophers' objection to tangency proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' objection to the atomist proof from tangency and how the author refutes it within the framework of kalam physics.

Core Idea
The point is an extremity, not a permeating accident — but that does not save the philosophers from atomism.

In this passage, the philosopher's objection to the second proof (the sphere and surface) is presented and then refuted by the author. The philosophers argue that the principle of accident division only applies to permeating accidents, not to points. The author mounts a sharp counter-argument, showing that the philosophers' own geometrical principles lead to absurdities if they deny indivisible points. This lesson unpacks that exchange.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation to get the overall flow of the argument.
Pay attention to the technical terms like 'saryan' (permeation) and 'nokta' (point).
2
Identify the philosophers' claim
Locate the conditional statement: division of accident only if permeation. Understand their distinction between permeation and being an extremity.
3
Analyze the author's response
The author says the sphere-surface tangency argument is strong. Trace his reasoning: why the place of contact cannot be divisible, and the consequences if it were.
The response uses reductio ad absurdum — if divisible, point becomes line or surface, sphere becomes polygonal.
4
Connect to the broader proof
See how this refutation defends the necessity of indivisible atoms, which is the main goal of the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحكماء يزعمون أن انقسام الحال بانقسام المحل مختص بما يكون حلوله بطريق السريان، كالبياض في الجسم. والنقطة إنما تحل في الخط من حيث أنها نهاية له لا سارية فيه، وكذا الخط في السطح، والسطح في الجسم التعليمي الحال في الجسم الطبيعي بطريق السريان. والحق أن حديث الكرة والسطح قوي و تماسهما بجوهر بهما ضروري والقول بأن موضع التماس منقسم بالفرض يخالف قواعدهم، لأن معناه صحة فرض شيء غير شيء، وهذا في النقطة محال، به يصير خطاً أو سطحاً مستوياً ضرورة الانطباق على السطح المستوى، وعند زوال التماس من ذلك الموضع إلى موضع آخر يصير الكرة من ذوات الأضلاع، على أن النقطة عندهم إنما هي النهاية للخط فلا توجد في الكرة بالفعل.
The philosophers (الحكماء) claim that the division of an accident with the division of its subject is specific to what inheres by way of permeation (بطريق السريان), like whiteness in a body. The point only inheres in the line as its extremity, not permeating in it, and likewise the line in the surface, and the surface in the mathematical body (الجسم التعليمي) which inheres in the natural body by way of permeation. The truth is that the account of the sphere and surface is strong, and their touching by a substance is necessary for both, and the statement that the place of contact is divisible by hypothesis contradicts their principles, because its meaning is the validity of assuming something other than something, and this is impossible in the point, for by it it would become a line or plane due to necessity of coincidence with the plane, and when contact ceases from that position to another, the sphere becomes polygonal, even though the point according to them is only the extremity of the line and does not exist in the sphere in actuality.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage presents the philosophers' (الحكماء) objection to the second proof (the sphere and surface) and the author's response. The philosophers argue that the principle 'the accident divides with the division of its subject' only applies when the accident inheres by permeation (سريان), like whiteness in a body. The point, however, is not permeating; it is merely the extremity of the line. Similarly, the line is the extremity of the surface, and the surface is the extremity of the mathematical body, itself permeating the natural body. Therefore, the point does not necessarily divide with the line. The author (الحق) counters that the sphere-surface tangency argument is sound and that contact must occur at an indivisible substance. To claim the contact area is divisible (even hypothetically) contradicts geometrical principles, because it would mean that the point could become a line or plane by coincidence with the plane, making the sphere polygonal upon movement. Moreover, the philosophers themselves admit that the point is only an extremity, not actually existing in the sphere, which undermines their objection. Thus the author defends the necessity of indivisible atoms.

Key Terms
حكماء
سريان
نقطة
جوهر
كرة
سطح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The philosophers' objection successfully shows that the tangency proof does not require indivisible atoms.
Correction: The author demonstrates that even if the point is not permeating, the geometry of tangency still forces indivisibility, otherwise contradictions arise.

Checkpoint
According to the philosophers in this passage, when does an accident divide with its subject?
A) When it inheres by permeation.
B) When it is a point.
C) When it is a substance.
D) Always.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers' distinction between permeating and non-permeating accidents does not salvage their position; the tangency proof remains valid for atomism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When the philosophers tried to evade the truth by splitting hairs (permeating vs. non-permeating), the author's refutation held them accountable to logical consistency. Where in your own life do you make convenient distinctions to avoid facing a truth you know is inevitable? Will you allow that defense to crumble under honest examination today?
?
The author argues that if the point of contact between the sphere and surface could be divided, absurdities would follow. Consider your own core beliefs: if you allow them to be subtly eroded by seemingly clever objections, what absurdities in your character or actions will eventually follow? What specific step will you take to guard against rationalisations?
?
The philosophers defined the point as a mere extremity, not an actual existent, yet their definition did not save them from the necessity of indivisible substance. You may define your commitments as 'just intellectual' or 'not applying to my daily life,' but does your actual life reveal otherwise? What one area of your practice contradicts your stated beliefs, and when will you close that gap?

Euclid's Proof of the Indivisible Tangent Angle
Euclid's geometric proof of indivisibility of tangent angle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Euclid's geometric argument that the tangent angle is the smallest possible and therefore indivisible, leading to the conclusion that such an indivisible must be either a substance or an accident.

Core Idea
The tangent angle is smallest; dividing it would create a smaller angle—thus it is indivisible.

Euclid's proof is a classic example of using geometry to argue for the existence of indivisibles. In this passage, he demonstrates that the angle formed by a tangent line and a circle's circumference cannot be divided, because if it were, its half would be even smaller, contradicting its minimality. This leads to a crucial metaphysical conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read Euclid's argument
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the logical flow from premise to conclusion.
The argument is concise—each step builds on the last.
2
Identify the logical steps
Trace the reasoning: (1) tangent angle is smallest, (2) therefore it cannot be divided, (3) if it could, its half would be smaller, contradiction.
3
Understand the conclusion
Euclid concludes that the indivisible something must be either a substance or an accident. Consider what this implies for the nature of points.
This conclusion is the 'desired result' (المطلوب).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع : أنه برهـن أقليدس (۱) على أن الزاوية الحاصلة مماسة الخط المستقيم لمحيط الدائرة أصغر ما يمكن من الزوايا، فبالضرورة لا يقبل الانقسام، وإلا لكان نصفها أصغر منه ، فذلك الأمر الغير المنقسم، إما جوهر أو حال فيه ، وفيه المطلوب. والحكماء يزعمون أن انقسام الحال بانقسام المحل مختص بما يكون حلوله بطريق السريان، كالبياض في الجسم. والنقطة إنما تحل في الخط من حيث أنها نهاية له (۲) لا سارية فيه، وكذا الخط في السطح، والسطح في الجسم التعليمي الحال في الجسم الطبيعي بطريق السريان. والحق أن حديث الكرة والسطح قوي و تماسهما بجوهر بهما ضروري والقول بأن موضع التماس منقسم بالفرض يخالف قواعدهم، لأن معناه صحة فرض شيء غير شيء، وهذا في النقطة محال، به يصير خطاً أو سطحاً مستوياً ضرورة الانطباق على السطح المستوى، وعند زوال التماس من ذلك الموضع إلى موضع آخر يصير الكرة من ذوات الأضلاع، على أن النقطة عندهم إنما هي النهاية للخط فلا توجد في الكرة بالفعل.
Fourth: That Euclid's proof (1) that the angle resulting from the tangent of the straight line to the circumference of the circle is the smallest possible angle, so necessarily it does not accept division; otherwise its half would be smaller than it. So that indivisible thing is either a substance or an accident residing in it, and in this is the desired conclusion. The philosophers claim that the division of the accident by the division of the locus is specific to what has resolution by way of permeation (saryān), like whiteness in a body. The point only inheres in the line insofar as it is a termination (nihāya) for it, not permeating in it. Similarly, the line in the surface, and the surface in the teaching body (jism ta‘līmī) which inheres in the natural body by way of permeation. The truth is that the discourse regarding the sphere and the surface is strong, and their contact by a substance is necessary for them both. The statement that the place of contact is divisible by hypothesis contradicts their principles, because its meaning is the soundness of positing something other than something, and this regarding the point is impossible; by it it becomes a line or a plane surface necessarily by coincidence (inṭibāq) with the plane surface. And when contact ceases from that position to another position, the sphere becomes polygonal. Moreover, the point according to them is only the termination of the line, so it does not exist in the sphere in actuality.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage presents a geometric proof by Euclid for the indivisibility of the point of tangency, followed by the philosophers' refutation. Euclid's argument begins with the claim that the angle formed by the tangent line and the circumference of a circle is the smallest possible angle. If it were divisible, its half would be even smaller, contradicting its minimality. Thus, the angle is indivisible, and this indivisible thing must be either a substance or an accident. The philosophers respond that the division of an accident with its locus only applies when the accident permeates the locus, like whiteness in a body, but the point in the line is not permeating; it is a termination. Similarly, the line is a termination of the surface, and the surface of the teaching body which permeates the natural body. The author then declares the truth: the contact between a sphere and a surface is strong and necessarily involves a substance for both. The claim that the contact point is divisible by hypothesis contradicts philosophical principles because it would imply the possibility of positing another point, which is impossible for a point. Moreover, if contact moves, the sphere would become polygonal. Finally, the point according to the philosophers is only the termination of a line, so it does not actually exist in the sphere.

مماسة (tangent)
انقسام (division)
جوهر (substance)
حال (accident)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the angle itself is a physical substance.
Correction: Euclid's argument does not claim the angle is a substance; it claims the indivisible thing (the point of tangency) is either substance or accident.

Checkpoint

B) It is the smallest possible angle
C) It is defined by a straight line
D) It is a right angle

Key Takeaway
Euclid's proof shows that the smallest possible angle cannot be divided, leading to an indivisible entity that must be either a substance or an accident.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Euclid's proof shows that the smallest possible angle cannot be divided. In your life, have you been trying to 'divide' your commitment to truth by making exceptions? Where are you accepting a 'half' when the whole is required? What one compromise will you retract today?
?
The indivisible entity is either a substance or an accident. Reflect on your own essence: Are you living as a substance (independent, purposeful) or as a mere accident (reactive, superficial)? What single change can you make today to embody substance?
?
If the tangent angle is indivisible, then there are limits to what can be broken down. What belief have you been 'dividing' (compromising) that should remain whole and pure? Will you defend its integrity from now on, even if it costs you?

Philosophers' Objection: Permeation vs Termination
Philosophers' distinction between permeation and termination in inherence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' distinction between an accident that inheres by permeation and one that inheres as a termination, and why this distinction undermines Euclid's conclusion.

Core Idea
Division of accident requires permeation; the point is a termination, not a permeating accident.

The philosophers respond to Euclid by refining the concept of inherence. They argue that only accidents that permeate their locus (like whiteness in a body) divide when the locus divides. The point, however, inheres in the line as a termination, not through permeation, so it does not divide with the line.

Guided Path
1
Read the philosophers' claim
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice the general rule they state about division of accidents.
The rule is: 'division of the accident by division of the locus is specific to what has resolution by way of permeation.'
2
Identify the permeation vs termination distinction
They contrast 'permeation' (saryan) with 'termination' (nihaya). Whiteness permeates a body, but the point is only the termination of a line.
3
Apply to the point
Because the point is a termination, it does not divide when the line divides. This refutes Euclid's assumption that the indivisible point must be a substance or accident that divides.
This is a key objection in kalam debates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

Will you let that distinction redefine your priorities today?

Author's Truth: Sphere-Surface Contact Indivisible
Author's defense of indivisibility of sphere-surface contact point.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's defense of the indivisibility of the contact point between a sphere and a surface, and why the philosophers' own principles lead to contradictions if it were divisible.

Core Idea
Contact point is indivisible; if divisible, the sphere would become polygonal.

The author affirms the strength of the geometric argument for the indivisibility of the contact point between a sphere and a plane surface. He then refutes a potential objection: if the contact point were divisible by hypothesis, it would imply the possibility of another point, which is impossible for a point. Moreover, moving the contact would make the sphere polygonal, contradicting its nature.

Guided Path
1
Read the author's truth claim
Read the Arabic and translation. The author declares the sphere-surface contact argument is strong and that contact requires a substance.
The author sides with the geometric argument over the philosophers' objection.
2
Examine the objection and refutation
The objection says the contact point could be divisible by hypothesis. The author refutes this: it would mean being able to posit another point, which is impossible for a point; also it would make the sphere polygonal.
3
Understand the final point
The author reminds that for the philosophers, the point is only a termination of a line, so it does not actually exist in the sphere (as a real entity).
This reinforces their own definition.

Third Argument: Three Parts in Contact
Taftazani gives the third argument for divisibility of the atom from three contiguous parts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third argument for the divisibility of the atom based on three parts in contact, and its two logical consequences.

Core Idea
The middle part must either have distinct faces or be superfluous—both prove divisibility.

Taftazani presents a clever conditional argument: if three atoms are lined up, the middle one either prevents the outer ones from touching or it doesn't. Both possibilities lead to the conclusion that atoms must be divisible. Let's examine the logic carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Start by reading the original Arabic passage and its literal translation. Get a feel for the logical flow.
2
Understand the setup
Imagine three indivisible parts in a line: left, middle, right. The middle is between the other two, touching each. This is the scenario.
Note that this is a thought experiment.
3
Follow the first branch
If the middle part prevents the outer two from touching, then its face toward the left must be different from its face toward the right. That means the middle part has at least two distinct faces, implying it is divisible.
This branch leads directly to division.
4
Follow the second branch
If the middle part does not prevent them, then the outer two would meet and combine, creating a volume from just the two outer parts. But that would make the middle part unnecessary, and repeating this would prevent the formation of any body. This contradicts the existence of bodies, so this branch is impossible.
Thus both branches lead to the conclusion that the atom must be divisible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث : أنه إذا تماست ثلاثة أجزاء على الترتيب بأن يكون واحد منها بين اثنين، فالوسطاني إما أن يمنع الآخرين عن التلاقي والتماس، فيكون وجهه الذي يلاقي أحدهما غير الذي يلاقي الآخر، فينقسم . وإما أن لا يمنعهما فلا يحصل من اجتماع الجزئين حجم ومقدار وهكذا في الثالث والرابع ، فلا يحصل الحجم.
The third: that when three parts are in contact in order such that one of them is between two, then the middle one either prevents the other two from meeting and contact, so its face that meets one is not the face that meets the other, so it divides. Or it does not prevent them, so from the meeting of the two parts no volume or magnitude results, and likewise in the third and fourth, so no volume results.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof against the indivisible part (al-juz' alladhi la yatajzza'). It is a conditional argument. Consider three parts arranged in a line with the middle one between the other two. Two scenarios are possible. First, if the middle part prevents the outer two from touching each other, then its face that contacts one outer part must be different from its face that contacts the other outer part, because if the same face were contacting both, they would touch each other. Thus the middle part has two distinct faces, meaning it has parts (i.e., is divisible). Second, if the middle part does not prevent them, then the two outer parts would meet and combine, producing a volume. But then the middle part would be superfluous, and the size would come from the outer two alone, which are assumed indivisible. Repeating this, no aggregate volume would form, which contradicts the existence of a body. Therefore, the indivisible part must be divisible.

Key Terms
الجزء الذي لا يتجزأ
الانقسام
التماس
الحجم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the argument assumes the middle part must have distinct faces without justification.
Correction: The argument does not assume distinct faces; it derives them as a necessary consequence if the middle part prevents the outer two from touching. If the faces were the same, the outer two would touch, contradicting prevention.

Checkpoint
In the third argument, if the middle part prevents the outer two from touching, what follows?
A) The middle part is indivisible
B) The middle part has two different faces and thus divides
C) The two outer parts create a volume
D) The three parts remain in contact without division

Key Takeaway
The third argument shows that any attempt to conceive of an indivisible atom in a line of three leads to its divisibility or a contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Everything you see — including your own body — is made of parts that are infinitely divisible. Does that make you feel insignificant, or does it fill you with awe at the Creator who holds every tiny particle in existence? Will you take one minute before sleeping tonight to literally feel your hand and remember that each cell, each atom, is a sign of Allah?
?
The argument shows that if a middle particle did not serve its purpose of preventing contact, it would be superfluous. Do you ever feel like you are just 'there', not fulfilling your purpose? What is the one thing you know Allah wants from you right now, and what will you do about it today?
?
This logical proof is meant to strengthen certainty in Allah's existence. How many times have you heard proofs like this and still allowed doubts to creep in? What concrete step will you take to internalize one proof deeply this week, so that it transforms your trust in Allah from intellectual to heartfelt?
